Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

# Security Reachability Analysis: Envoy Admin Interface

## Scenario

You are performing a security audit of Envoy Proxy's administration interface. During static analysis, you identified a function with potentially dangerous operations:

**Function**: `AdminImpl::handlerDrainListeners()` in `source/server/admin/admin.cc`

This function handles the `/drain_listeners` endpoint, which forcibly drains all active listeners, closing existing connections and rejecting new ones. The implementation modifies critical server state and could be used for denial-of-service attacks.

## Your Task

Determine whether this function is **exploitable from external HTTP input** (i.e., from the internet-facing data plane). Specifically:

1. **Trace the call path**: Identify all code paths from external HTTP request reception to `handlerDrainListeners()`
2. **Identify protection mechanisms**: Is this endpoint restricted to specific network interfaces, ports, or authentication?
3. **Assess exploitability**: Can an external attacker reach this function? Or is it isolated to internal/admin-only access?
4. **Document the access control model**: What prevents external traffic from triggering admin endpoints?

## Codebase Context

- **Repository**: envoyproxy/envoy @ v1.31.1
- **Language**: C++
- **Focus Area**: Admin interface architecture and access control

## Background: Admin Interface vs Data Plane

Envoy has two separate network interfaces:

1. **Data Plane** (e.g., port 8080): Processes customer/external HTTP traffic
   - Configured via `listeners` in envoy.yaml
   - Typically bound to 0.0.0.0 or public IP
   - Handles production traffic

2. **Admin Interface** (e.g., port 9901): Debug and management endpoints
   - Configured via `admin` section in envoy.yaml
   - Typically bound to 127.0.0.1 (localhost only)
   - NOT meant for external access

## Expected Deliverable

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/triage.md`.

Include enough evidence to support your exploitability conclusion, including:
- the full call chain from request reception to the target handler
- the boundary between data-plane and admin-plane request handling
- the controls that prevent or permit external reachability
- the network/configuration conditions under which the endpoint would become externally reachable

## Important Notes

- Focus on **reachability analysis**, not on fixing the vulnerability
- Use static analysis and code review techniques
- Consider both HTTP/1.1 and HTTP/2 code paths
- Document your reasoning and evidence for each conclusion
- Be specific about validation checks (don't just say "input is validated" - cite the specific check and where it occurs)

## Success Criteria

Your analysis will be scored on:
- Correct identification of all call paths (25%)
- Accurate identification of protection mechanisms (30%)
- Correct exploitability assessment (25%)
- Quality of evidence and reasoning (20%)

71-usertool_resultmcp__sourcegraph__sg_read_file
{"content":"1: .. _operations_admin_interface:\n2: \n3: Administration interface\n4: ========================\n5: \n6: Envoy exposes a local administration interface that can be used to query and\n7: modify different aspects of the server:\n8: \n9: * :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_config.bootstrap.v3.Admin>`\n10: \n11: .. _operations_admin_interface_security:\n12: \n13: .. attention::\n14: \n15:   The administration interface in its current form both allows destructive operations to be\n16:   performed (e.g., shutting down the server) as well as potentially exposes private information\n17:   (e.g., stats, cluster names, cert info, etc.). It is **critical** that access to the\n18:   administration interface is only allowed via a secure network. It is also **critical** that hosts\n19:   that access the administration interface are **only** attached to the secure network (i.e., to\n20:   avoid CSRF attacks). This involves setting up an appropriate firewall or optimally only allowing\n21:   access to the administration listener via localhost. 103-assistanttext-
The analysis is complete and written to `/logs/agent/triage.md`. Here's a summary of the key findings:

**Exploitability: NOT exploitable from external HTTP input under default configuration.**

The analysis traced the complete call chain from request reception to `handlerDrainListeners()` and identified the architectural boundary between admin and data plane:

1. **Separate listener sockets**: Admin binds to its own TCP socket (conventionally `127.0.0.1:9901`), completely independent from data-plane listener sockets.

2. **Separate filter chains**: Admin connections get `AdminFilter` installed via `AdminImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()`, while data-plane connections get operator-configured filter chains via `ListenerImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()`. There is no code path connecting them.

3. **Separate request routing**: Admin uses prefix-matching against a hardcoded handler list (`AdminImpl::makeRequest()`), while data-plane uses RDS/static route configuration to route to upstream clusters.

4. **Protection mechanisms identified**:
   - Localhost binding (primary, network-level)
   - POST method enforcement for mutating endpoints
   - Optional `allow_paths` allowlist (returns 403 for unlisted paths)
   - No authentication or TLS (documented gap)

5. **Risk**: Low under default config, but becomes critical if the admin interface is misconfigured to bind to `0.0.0.0` or a public IP, since there is no built-in authentication.

  "content": "# Security Reachability Analysis: `handlerDrainListeners()` via Envoy Admin Interface\n\n## 1. Executive Summary\n\n**Target function:** `ListenersHandler::handlerDrainListeners()` in `source/server/admin/listeners_handler.cc:15`\n\n**Exploitability assessment: NOT exploitable from the external data plane under default configuration.**\n\nThe `/drain_listeners` endpoint is served exclusively by Envoy's admin interface, which operates on a completely separate TCP listener from the data plane. The admin listener binds to its own address/port (conventionally `127.0.0.1:9901`) and has its own independent HTTP connection manager, filter chain, and request routing. There is no code path through which an HTTP request arriving on a data-plane listener can be routed to admin handler functions. However, if an operator misconfigures the admin interface to bind to `0.0.0.0` or a public IP, the endpoint becomes network-reachable from external sources, as there is no built-in authentication.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Full Call Chain: External Request to `handlerDrainListeners()`\n\n### 2.1 Admin-Plane Call Chain (the only path to the handler)\n\n```\n1. TCP connection arrives on admin listener socket\n   (AdminImpl::startHttpListener creates the socket)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:54-77\n\n2. ConnectionHandlerImpl dispatches the connection to the AdminListener\n   (bound via AdminImpl::addListenerToHandler \u2192 handler->addListener)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:549-554\n   \u2192 source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.cc:40-114\n\n3. ActiveTcpListener::onAccept() accepts the TCP connection\n   \u2192 source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80\n\n4. AdminImpl::findFilterChain() returns AdminFilterChain\n   (AdminImpl acts as Network::FilterChainManager)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.h:105-108\n\n5. AdminImpl::createNetworkFilterChain() installs Http::ConnectionManagerImpl\n   as the read filter, configured with AdminImpl as its ConnectionManagerConfig\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:302-312\n\n6. Http::ConnectionManagerImpl processes the HTTP request,\n   calls AdminImpl::createFilterChain() which installs AdminFilter\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:314-318\n\n7. AdminFilter::decodeHeaders() / onComplete() is called when request is received\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin_filter.cc:10-17, 83-107\n\n8. AdminFilter::onComplete() calls admin_.makeRequest(*this)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin_filter.cc:89\n\n9. AdminImpl::makeRequest() does prefix-matching on the request path\n   against the handlers_ list, finds \"/drain_listeners\"\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:400-437\n\n10. The handler for \"/drain_listeners\" is\n    MAKE_ADMIN_HANDLER(listeners_handler_.handlerDrainListeners)\n    registered at admin.cc:214-226\n\n11. ListenersHandler::handlerDrainListeners() executes\n    \u2192 source/server/admin/listeners_handler.cc:15-57\n```\n\n### 2.2 Data-Plane Call Chain (does NOT reach admin handlers)\n\n```\n1. TCP connection arrives on a data-plane listener socket\n   (configured via `listeners` section in bootstrap/xDS)\n\n2. ConnectionHandlerImpl dispatches to the data-plane ListenerImpl\n\n3. ListenerImpl::createNetworkFilterChain() builds the\n   operator-configured filter chain (e.g., HCM + router)\n   \u2192 source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.cc:959-969\n\n4. Http::ConnectionManagerImpl is configured with the\n   data-plane's RouteConfigProvider, which routes to\n   upstream clusters \u2014 NOT to admin handlers\n\n5. There is NO path from a data-plane HCM to AdminImpl::makeRequest()\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Architectural Boundary: Admin Plane vs. Data Plane\n\n### 3.1 Separate Listener Sockets\n\nThe admin interface and data-plane listeners bind to **completely independent TCP sockets**:\n\n- **Admin socket**: Created in `AdminImpl::startHttpListener()` (`source/server/admin/admin.cc:59`):\n  ```cpp\n  socket_ = std::make_shared<Network::TcpListenSocket>(address, socket_options, true);\n  ```\n  The `address` comes from `initial_config.admin().address()`, which is parsed from the `admin.address` field in the bootstrap configuration (`source/server/configuration_impl.cc:257-263`).\n\n- **Data-plane sockets**: Created by `ListenerManagerImpl::createListenSocket()` for each listener in the `listeners` configuration section (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.cc:325-394`).\n\nThese are separate OS-level TCP sockets bound to different addresses/ports. A TCP connection arriving on port 8080 (data plane) can never be dispatched to the admin listener on port 9901.\n\n### 3.2 Separate Filter Chains\n\n- **Admin**: `AdminImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()` (`admin.cc:302-312`) installs `Http::ConnectionManagerImpl` configured with `AdminImpl` itself as the `ConnectionManagerConfig`. This HCM's `filterFactory()` returns `AdminImpl`, whose `createFilterChain()` installs `AdminFilter` \u2014 the only filter that can invoke `AdminImpl::makeRequest()`.\n\n- **Data plane**: `ListenerImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()` (`listener_impl.cc:959-969`) builds from operator-configured `NetworkFilterFactoriesList`, typically including an HCM configured with route tables pointing to upstream clusters.\n\n### 3.3 Separate Request Routing\n\n- **Admin**: `AdminImpl::makeRequest()` (`admin.cc:400-437`) does prefix matching against a hardcoded list of admin `UrlHandler` objects (e.g., `/drain_listeners`, `/stats`, `/clusters`).\n\n- **Data plane**: `Http::ConnectionManagerImpl` uses `RouteConfigProvider` to resolve routes via RDS/static route configuration to upstream clusters.\n\nThere is **no shared routing table** and **no mechanism** for data-plane routes to delegate to admin handlers.\n\n### 3.4 Shared ConnectionHandler, but Isolated Listeners\n\nBoth admin and data-plane listeners are added to the same `ConnectionHandlerImpl` instance (`handler_` in `source/server/server.cc:794`). However, `ConnectionHandlerImpl` dispatches incoming connections to listeners based on which socket accepted the connection. Each `ActiveTcpListener` is associated with a specific socket, so connections are routed to the correct listener based on the accepting socket. This is socket-level isolation \u2014 a connection accepted on the admin socket will only ever be handled by the admin listener's filter chain.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Protection Mechanisms\n\n### 4.1 Network-Level: Bind Address (Primary Protection)\n\nThe recommended and primary protection is binding the admin interface to `127.0.0.1` (localhost):\n\n```yaml\nadmin:\n  address:\n    socket_address: { address: 127.0.0.1, port_value: 9901 }\n```\n\nThis is documented in `docs/root/operations/admin.rst:13-32`:\n> It is **critical** that access to the administration interface is only allowed via a secure network.\n\nThe bind address is specified in the bootstrap config (`api/envoy/config/bootstrap/v3/bootstrap.proto:459-461`):\n```protobuf\n// The TCP address that the administration server will listen on.\n// If not specified, Envoy will not start an administration server.\ncore.v3.Address address = 3;\n```\n\nIf no address is specified, the admin server is **not started at all** (`source/server/server.cc:786-788`):\n```cpp\n} else {\n    ENVOY_LOG(info, \"No admin address given, so no admin HTTP server started.\");\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 HTTP Method Enforcement\n\nMutating endpoints like `/drain_listeners` require HTTP POST. The handler is registered with `mutates_server_state_ = true` (`admin.cc:215`). The enforcement occurs in `AdminImpl::makeRequest()` (`admin.cc:415-424`):\n\n```cpp\nif (handler.mutates_server_state_) {\n    const absl::string_view method = admin_stream.getRequestHeaders().getMethodValue();\n    if (method != Http::Headers::get().MethodValues.Post) {\n        return Admin::makeStaticTextRequest(\n            fmt::format(\"Method {} not allowed, POST required.\", method),\n            Http::Code::MethodNotAllowed);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis prevents GET-based CSRF attacks against state-mutating endpoints.\n\n### 4.3 Path Allowlisting (`allow_paths`)\n\nThe `Admin` protobuf message supports an `allow_paths` field (`bootstrap.proto:471-484`) that restricts which admin endpoints are accessible:\n\n```protobuf\nrepeated type.matcher.v3.StringMatcher allow_paths = 7;\n```\n\nWhen configured, `AdminImpl::makeRequest()` checks the path against the allowlist before dispatching (`admin.cc:406-411`):\n\n```cpp\nif (!allowlisted_paths_.empty() && !acceptTargetPath(path_and_query)) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(info, \"Request to admin interface path {} is not allowed\", path_and_query);\n    return Admin::makeStaticTextRequest(error_response, Http::Code::Forbidden);\n}\n```\n\nIf `allow_paths` is configured and `/drain_listeners` is not in the list, the endpoint returns HTTP 403 Forbidden. The allowlist is populated at server initialization (`server.cc:656-659`).\n\n### 4.4 No Authentication / No TLS\n\nThe admin interface uses `RawBufferSocketFactory` (plaintext, no TLS) as its transport socket (`admin.h:467`):\n```cpp\nconst Network::RawBufferSocketFactory transport_socket_factory_;\n```\n\nThere is **no built-in authentication mechanism** (no basic auth, no mTLS, no API keys). The `AdminInternalAddressConfig` explicitly marks all addresses as non-internal (`admin.h:58-60`):\n```cpp\nclass AdminInternalAddressConfig : public Http::InternalAddressConfig {\n    bool isInternalAddress(const Network::Address::Instance&) const override { return false; }\n};\n```\n\n### 4.5 XSS Prevention in Handler Registration\n\nAdmin handler paths are sanitized to prevent XSS injection (`admin.cc:495-498`):\n```cpp\nconst std::string::size_type pos = prefix.find_first_of(\"&\\\"'<>?:\");\nif (pos != std::string::npos) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(error, \"filter \\\"{}\\\" contains invalid character '{}'\", prefix, prefix[pos]);\n    return false;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Exploitability Assessment\n\n### 5.1 Default Configuration: NOT Exploitable\n\nUnder the recommended configuration (`admin.address: 127.0.0.1:9901`):\n\n1. **Network isolation**: The admin socket is bound to localhost. External traffic cannot reach it at the OS level.\n2. **Listener isolation**: Even if an attacker reaches the data-plane port, the connection is handled by a completely different filter chain with no path to admin handlers.\n3. **No request routing crossover**: Data-plane HCM routes to upstream clusters; it has no route entries pointing to admin endpoints.\n\nAn external attacker on the internet **cannot** reach `handlerDrainListeners()`.\n\n### 5.2 Misconfiguration Scenarios: Potentially Exploitable\n\nThe endpoint **becomes reachable** if:\n\n1. **Admin bound to `0.0.0.0` or public IP**: If the operator configures `admin.address` to `0.0.0.0:9901` or a publicly-routable IP, the admin interface accepts connections from any source. Since there is no authentication, any client that can reach the port can invoke `/drain_listeners` via POST.\n\n2. **No firewall/network policy**: Even with localhost binding, if an attacker has SSRF access from a co-located service that can reach `127.0.0.1:9901`, they can invoke admin endpoints.\n\n3. **Port forwarding or reverse proxy**: If an operator forwards the admin port through a load balancer or reverse proxy without authentication, the admin interface becomes externally accessible.\n\n### 5.3 Impact if Exploited\n\nIf `handlerDrainListeners()` is reached by an attacker:\n\n- **Without parameters**: Immediately stops all listeners (`server_.listenerManager().stopListeners()`), causing a complete denial of service.\n- **With `?graceful`**: Enters a drain period then stops listeners, causing a graceful but still complete DoS.\n- **With `?inboundonly`**: Stops only inbound listeners, still causing DoS for inbound traffic.\n- **With `?graceful&skip_exit`**: Drains connections but doesn't stop listeners \u2014 still disrupts active connections.\n\nThe attack requires only a single HTTP POST request: `POST /drain_listeners`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Summary of Controls\n\n| Control | Type | Effectiveness | Location |\n|---------|------|---------------|----------|\n| Separate listener socket | Architectural | Strong \u2014 prevents data-plane crossover | `admin.cc:59`, `server.cc:781-782` |\n| Separate filter chain | Architectural | Strong \u2014 admin filter only exists on admin listener | `admin.cc:302-318` |\n| Separate request routing | Architectural | Strong \u2014 no shared route tables | `admin.cc:400-437` |\n| Bind to localhost | Configuration | Strong (when applied) \u2014 OS-level network isolation | `bootstrap.proto:459-461` |\n| POST method requirement | Application | Moderate \u2014 prevents GET-based CSRF | `admin.cc:415-424` |\n| `allow_paths` allowlist | Configuration | Moderate (opt-in) \u2014 restricts accessible endpoints | `admin.cc:406-411`, `bootstrap.proto:471-484` |\n| No authentication | Gap | Weakness \u2014 anyone who can reach the port can use it | `admin.h:467` (RawBufferSocketFactory) |\n| No TLS | Gap | Weakness \u2014 traffic is unencrypted | `admin.h:467` |\n\n---\n\n## 7. Conclusion\n\nThe `handlerDrainListeners()` function is **not reachable from external HTTP input** under Envoy's default/recommended configuration. The admin interface is architecturally isolated from the data plane through separate listener sockets, separate filter chains, and separate request routing. The primary protection is the network-level binding of the admin socket to localhost.\n\nHowever, the admin interface lacks authentication and TLS, making it vulnerable to exploitation if misconfigured to listen on a publicly accessible address. The security model relies entirely on network-level access control (bind address + firewall rules), which is documented in Envoy's operations guide but is the operator's responsibility to enforce.\n\n**Risk rating: Low (default) / Critical (if misconfigured)**\n\nThe absence of built-in authentication means the security boundary is binary: either the admin port is network-unreachable from attackers (safe) or it is reachable (fully compromised, no defense in depth).\n",

However, if an operator misconfigures the admin interface to bind to `0.0.0.0` or a public IP, the endpoint becomes network-reachable from external sources, as there is no built-in authentication.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Full Call Chain: External Request to `handlerDrainListeners()`\n\n### 2.1 Admin-Plane Call Chain (the only path to the handler)\n\n```\n1. TCP connection arrives on admin listener socket\n   (AdminImpl::startHttpListener creates the socket)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:54-77\n\n2. ConnectionHandlerImpl dispatches the connection to the AdminListener\n   (bound via AdminImpl::addListenerToHandler \u2192 handler->addListener)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:549-554\n   \u2192 source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.cc:40-114\n\n3. ActiveTcpListener::onAccept() accepts the TCP connection\n   \u2192 source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80\n\n4. AdminImpl::findFilterChain() returns AdminFilterChain\n   (AdminImpl acts as Network::FilterChainManager)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.h:105-108\n\n5. AdminImpl::createNetworkFilterChain() installs Http::ConnectionManagerImpl\n   as the read filter, configured with AdminImpl as its ConnectionManagerConfig\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:302-312\n\n6. Http::ConnectionManagerImpl processes the HTTP request,\n   calls AdminImpl::createFilterChain() which installs AdminFilter\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:314-318\n\n7. AdminFilter::decodeHeaders() / onComplete() is called when request is received\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin_filter.cc:10-17, 83-107\n\n8. AdminFilter::onComplete() calls admin_.makeRequest(*this)\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin_filter.cc:89\n\n9. AdminImpl::makeRequest() does prefix-matching on the request path\n   against the handlers_ list, finds \"/drain_listeners\"\n   \u2192 source/server/admin/admin.cc:400-437\n\n10. The handler for \"/drain_listeners\" is\n    MAKE_ADMIN_HANDLER(listeners_handler_.handlerDrainListeners)\n    registered at admin.cc:214-226\n\n11. ListenersHandler::handlerDrainListeners() executes\n    \u2192 source/server/admin/listeners_handler.cc:15-57\n```\n\n### 2.2 Data-Plane Call Chain (does NOT reach admin handlers)\n\n```\n1. TCP connection arrives on a data-plane listener socket\n   (configured via `listeners` section in bootstrap/xDS)\n\n2. ConnectionHandlerImpl dispatches to the data-plane ListenerImpl\n\n3. ListenerImpl::createNetworkFilterChain() builds the\n   operator-configured filter chain (e.g., HCM + router)\n   \u2192 source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.cc:959-969\n\n4. Http::ConnectionManagerImpl is configured with the\n   data-plane's RouteConfigProvider, which routes to\n   upstream clusters \u2014 NOT to admin handlers\n\n5. There is NO path from a data-plane HCM to AdminImpl::makeRequest()\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Architectural Boundary: Admin Plane vs. Data Plane\n\n### 3.1 Separate Listener Sockets\n\nThe admin interface and data-plane listeners bind to **completely independent TCP sockets**:\n\n- **Admin socket**: Created in `AdminImpl::startHttpListener()` (`source/server/admin/admin.cc:59`):\n  ```cpp\n  socket_ = std::make_shared<Network::TcpListenSocket>(address, socket_options, true);\n  ```\n  The `address` comes from `initial_config.admin().address()`, which is parsed from the `admin.address` field in the bootstrap configuration (`source/server/configuration_impl.cc:257-263`).\n\n- **Data-plane sockets**: Created by `ListenerManagerImpl::createListenSocket()` for each listener in the `listeners` configuration section (`source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.cc:325-394`).\n\nThese are separate OS-level TCP sockets bound to different addresses/ports. A TCP connection arriving on port 8080 (data plane) can never be dispatched to the admin listener on port 9901.\n\n### 3.2 Separate Filter Chains\n\n- **Admin**: `AdminImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()` (`admin.cc:302-312`) installs `Http::ConnectionManagerImpl` configured with `AdminImpl` itself as the `ConnectionManagerConfig`. This HCM's `filterFactory()` returns `AdminImpl`, whose `createFilterChain()` installs `AdminFilter` \u2014 the only filter that can invoke `AdminImpl::makeRequest()`.\n\n- **Data plane**: `ListenerImpl::createNetworkFilterChain()` (`listener_impl.cc:959-969`) builds from operator-configured `NetworkFilterFactoriesList`, typically including an HCM configured with route tables pointing to upstream clusters.\n\n### 3.3 Separate Request Routing\n\n- **Admin**: `AdminImpl::makeRequest()` (`admin.cc:400-437`) does prefix matching against a hardcoded list of admin `UrlHandler` objects (e.g., `/drain_listeners`, `/stats`, `/clusters`).\n\n- **Data plane**: `Http::ConnectionManagerImpl` uses `RouteConfigProvider` to resolve routes via RDS/static route configuration to upstream clusters.\n\nThere is **no shared routing table** and **no mechanism** for data-plane routes to delegate to admin handlers.\n\n### 3.4 Shared ConnectionHandler, but Isolated Listeners\n\nBoth admin and data-plane listeners are added to the same `ConnectionHandlerImpl` instance (`handler_` in `source/server/server.cc:794`). However, `ConnectionHandlerImpl` dispatches incoming connections to listeners based on which socket accepted the connection. Each `ActiveTcpListener` is associated with a specific socket, so connections are routed to the correct listener based on the accepting socket. This is socket-level isolation \u2014 a connection accepted on the admin socket will only ever be handled by the admin listener's filter chain.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Protection Mechanisms\n\n### 4.1 Network-Level: Bind Address (Primary Protection)\n\nThe recommended and primary protection is binding the admin interface to `127.0.0.1` (localhost):\n\n```yaml\nadmin:\n  address:\n    socket_address: { address: 127.0.0.1, port_value: 9901 }\n```\n\nThis is documented in `docs/root/operations/admin.rst:13-32`:\n> It is **critical** that access to the administration interface is only allowed via a secure network.\n\nThe bind address is specified in the bootstrap config (`api/envoy/config/bootstrap/v3/bootstrap.proto:459-461`):\n```protobuf\n// The TCP address that the administration server will listen on.\n// If not specified, Envoy will not start an administration server.\ncore.v3.Address address = 3;\n```\n\nIf no address is specified, the admin server is **not started at all** (`source/server/server.cc:786-788`):\n```cpp\n} else {\n    ENVOY_LOG(info, \"No admin address given, so no admin HTTP server started.\");\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 HTTP Method Enforcement\n\nMutating endpoints like `/drain_listeners` require HTTP POST. The handler is registered with `mutates_server_state_ = true` (`admin.cc:215`). The enforcement occurs in `AdminImpl::makeRequest()` (`admin.cc:415-424`):\n\n```cpp\nif (handler.mutates_server_state_) {\n    const absl::string_view method = admin_stream.getRequestHeaders().getMethodValue();\n    if (method != Http::Headers::get().MethodValues.Post) {\n        return Admin::makeStaticTextRequest(\n            fmt::format(\"Method {} not allowed, POST required.\", method),\n            Http::Code::MethodNotAllowed);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis prevents GET-based CSRF attacks against state-mutating endpoints.\n\n### 4.3 Path Allowlisting (`allow_paths`)\n\nThe `Admin` protobuf message supports an `allow_paths` field (`bootstrap.proto:471-484`) that restricts which admin endpoints are accessible:\n\n```protobuf\nrepeated type.matcher.v3.StringMatcher allow_paths = 7;\n```\n\nWhen configured, `AdminImpl::makeRequest()` checks the path against the allowlist before dispatching (`admin.cc:406-411`):\n\n```cpp\nif (!allowlisted_paths_.empty() && !acceptTargetPath(path_and_query)) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(info, \"Request to admin interface path {} is not allowed\", path_and_query);\n    return Admin::makeStaticTextRequest(error_response, Http::Code::Forbidden);\n}\n```\n\nIf `allow_paths` is configured and `/drain_listeners` is not in the list, the endpoint returns HTTP 403 Forbidden. The allowlist is populated at server initialization (`server.cc:656-659`).\n\n### 4.4 No Authentication / No TLS\n\nThe admin interface uses `RawBufferSocketFactory` (plaintext, no TLS) as its transport socket (`admin.h:467`):\n```cpp\nconst Network::RawBufferSocketFactory transport_socket_factory_;\n```\n\nThere is **no built-in authentication mechanism** (no basic auth, no mTLS, no API keys). The `AdminInternalAddressConfig` explicitly marks all addresses as non-internal (`admin.h:58-60`):\n```cpp\nclass AdminInternalAddressConfig : public Http::InternalAddressConfig {\n    bool isInternalAddress(const Network::Address::Instance&) const override { return false; }\n};\n```\n\n### 4.5 XSS Prevention in Handler Registration\n\nAdmin handler paths are sanitized to prevent XSS injection (`admin.cc:495-498`):\n```cpp\nconst std::string::size_type pos = prefix.find_first_of(\"&\\\"'<>?:\");\nif (pos != std::string::npos) {\n    ENVOY_LOG(error, \"filter \\\"{}\\\" contains invalid character '{}'\", prefix, prefix[pos]);\n    return false;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Exploitability Assessment\n\n### 5.1 Default Configuration: NOT Exploitable\n\nUnder the recommended configuration (`admin.address: 127.0.0.1:9901`):\n\n1. **Network isolation**: The admin socket is bound to localhost. External traffic cannot reach it at the OS level.\n2. **Listener isolation**: Even if an attacker reaches the data-plane port, the connection is handled by a completely different filter chain with no path to admin handlers.\n3. **No request routing crossover**: Data-plane HCM routes to upstream clusters; it has no route entries pointing to admin endpoints.\n\nAn external attacker on the internet **cannot** reach `handlerDrainListeners()`.\n\n### 5.2 Misconfiguration Scenarios: Potentially Exploitable\n\nThe endpoint **becomes reachable** if:\n\n1. **Admin bound to `0.0.0.0` or public IP**: If the operator configures `admin.address` to `0.0.0.0:9901` or a publicly-routable IP, the admin interface accepts connections from any source. Since there is no authentication, any client that can reach the port can invoke `/drain_listeners` via POST.\n\n2. **No firewall/network policy**: Even with localhost binding, if an attacker has SSRF access from a co-located service that can reach `127.0.0.1:9901`, they can invoke admin endpoints.\n\n3. **Port forwarding or reverse proxy**: If an operator forwards the admin port through a load balancer or reverse proxy without authentication, the admin interface becomes externally accessible.\n\n### 5.3 Impact if Exploited\n\nIf `handlerDrainListeners()` is reached by an attacker:\n\n- **Without parameters**: Immediately stops all listeners (`server_.listenerManager().stopListeners()`), causing a complete denial of service.\n- **With `?graceful`**: Enters a drain period then stops listeners, causing a graceful but still complete DoS.\n- **With `?inboundonly`**: Stops only inbound listeners, still causing DoS for inbound traffic.\n- **With `?graceful&skip_exit`**: Drains connections but doesn't stop listeners \u2014 still disrupts active connections.\n\nThe attack requires only a single HTTP POST request: `POST /drain_listeners`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Summary of Controls\n\n| Control | Type | Effectiveness | Location |\n|---------|------|---------------|----------|\n| Separate listener socket | Architectural | Strong \u2014 prevents data-plane crossover | `admin.cc:59`, `server.cc:781-782` |\n| Separate filter chain | Architectural | Strong \u2014 admin filter only exists on admin listener | `admin.cc:302-318` |\n| Separate request routing | Architectural | Strong \u2014 no shared route tables | `admin.cc:400-437` |\n| Bind to localhost | Configuration | Strong (when applied) \u2014 OS-level network isolation | `bootstrap.proto:459-461` |\n| POST method requirement | Application | Moderate \u2014 prevents GET-based CSRF | `admin.cc:415-424` |\n| `allow_paths` allowlist | Configuration | Moderate (opt-in) \u2014 restricts accessible endpoints | `admin.cc:406-411`, `bootstrap.proto:471-484` |\n| No authentication | Gap | Weakness \u2014 anyone who can reach the port can use it | `admin.h:467` (RawBufferSocketFactory) |\n| No TLS | Gap | Weakness \u2014 traffic is unencrypted | `admin.h:467` |\n\n---\n\n## 7. Conclusion\n\nThe `handlerDrainListeners()` function is **not reachable from external HTTP input** under Envoy's default/recommended configuration. The admin interface is architecturally isolated from the data plane through separate listener sockets, separate filter chains, and separate request routing. The primary protection is the network-level binding of the admin socket to localhost.\n\nHowever, the admin interface lacks authentication and TLS, making it vulnerable to exploitation if misconfigured to listen on a publicly accessible address. The security model relies entirely on network-level access control (bind address + firewall rules), which is documented in Envoy's operations guide but is the operator's responsibility to enforce.\n\n**Risk rating: Low (default) / Critical (if misconfigured)**\n\nThe absence of built-in authentication means the security boundary is binary: either the admin port is network-unreachable from attackers (safe) or it is reachable (fully compromised, no defense in depth).\n",

# Security Reachability Analysis: `handlerDrainListeners()` via Envoy Admin Interface

## 1. Executive Summary

**Target function:** `ListenersHandler::handlerDrainListeners()` in `source/server/admin/listeners_handler.cc:15`

**Exploitability assessment: NOT exploitable from the external data plane under default configuration.**

The `/drain_listeners` endpoint is served exclusively by Envoy's admin interface, which operates on a completely separate TCP listener from the data plane. The admin listener binds to its own address/port (conventionally `127.0.0.1:9901`) and has its own independent HTTP connection manager, filter chain, and request routing. There is no code path through which an HTTP request arriving on a data-plane listener can be routed to admin handler functions. However, if an operator misconfigures the admin interface to bind to `0.0.0.0` or a public IP, the endpoint becomes network-reachable from external sources, as there is no built-in authentication.

---

## 2. Full Call Chain: External Request to `handlerDrainListeners()`

### 2.1 Admin-Plane Call Chain (the only path to the handler)

```
1. TCP connection arrives on admin listener socket
   (AdminImpl::startHttpListener creates the socket)
   → source/server/admin/admin.cc:54-77

2. ConnectionHandlerImpl dispatches the connection to the AdminListener
   (bound via AdminImpl::addListenerToHandler → handler->addListener)
   → source/server/admin/admin.cc:549-554
   → source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.cc:40-114

3. ActiveTcpListener::onAccept() accepts the TCP connection
   → source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.cc:80

4. AdminImpl::findFilterChain() returns AdminFilterChain
   (AdminImpl acts as Network::FilterChainManager)
   → source/server/admin/admin.h:105-108

... (truncated)
